            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-28 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-28">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>1.7 &#8212; Forward declarations</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on June 2nd, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>Take a look at this seemingly innocent sample program called add.cpp:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f455005224464" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0019 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>You would expect this program to produce the result:</p>
<pre>The sum of 3 and 4 is: 7</pre>
<p>But in fact, it doesn&#8217;t compile at all!  Visual Studio 2005 Express produces the following compile errors:</p>
<pre>
add.cpp(6) : error C3861: &#039;add&#039;: identifier not found
add.cpp(10) : error C2365: &#039;add&#039; : redefinition; previous definition was &#039;formerly unknown identifier&#039;
</pre>
<p>The reason this program doesn&#8217;t compile is because the compiler reads files sequentially.  When the compiler reaches the function call to add() on line 6 of main(), it doesn&#8217;t know what add is, because we haven&#8217;t defined add() until line 10!  That produces the first error (&#8220;identifier not found&#8221;).</p>
<p>When Visual Studio 2005 gets to the actual declaration of add() on line 10, it also complains about add being redefined.  This is somewhat misleading, given that it wasn&#8217;t ever defined in the first place.  Later versions of Visual Studio correctly omit this additional error message.</p>
<p>Despite the redundancy of the second error, it&#8217;s useful to note that it is fairly common for a single error to produce (often redundant) multiple compiler errors or warnings.</p>
<p><em>Rule: When addressing compile errors in your programs, always resolve the first error produced first.</em></p>
<p>To fix this problem, we need to address the fact that the compiler doesn&#8217;t know what add is.  There are two common ways to address the issue.</p>
<p>Option 1: Reorder the function calls so add() is defined before main():</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-10">10</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-11">11</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-12">12</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-13">13</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-3"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-4"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-8"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">using</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"The sum of 3 and 4 is: "</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-cn">3</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f468398326383-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0018 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>That way, by the time main() calls add(), the compiler will already know what add() is.  Because this is such a simple program, this change is relatively easy to do.  However, in a larger program, it can be tedious trying to figure out which functions call which other functions (and in what order) so they can be declared sequentially.</p>
<p>Furthermore, this option is not always possible.  Let&#8217;s say we&#8217;re writing a program that has two functions A and B.  If function A calls function B, and function B calls function A, then there&#8217;s no way to order the functions in a way that they will both be happy.  If you define A first, the compiler will complain it doesn&#8217;t know what B is.  If you define B first, the compiler will complain that it doesn&#8217;t know what A is.  </p>
<p><strong>Function prototypes and forward declarations of functions</strong></p>
<p>Option 2: Use a forward declaration.</p>
<p>A <strong>forward declaration</strong> allows us to tell the compiler that a function exists <em>before</em> defining what the function does.  This way, when the compiler encounters a call to the function, it&#8217;ll understand that we&#8217;re making a function call, and can check to ensure we&#8217;re calling the function correctly.</p>
<p>To write a forward declaration for a function, we use a declaration statement called a <strong>function prototype</strong>.  The function prototype consists of the function&#8217;s return type, name, parameters, but no function body (the part between the curly braces).  And because the function prototype is a statement, it ends with a semicolon.</p>
<p>Here&#8217;s a function prototype for the add() function:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f471824824184" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f471824824184-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f471824824184-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// function prototype includes return type, name, parameters, and semicolon.&nbsp;&nbsp;No function body!</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->

class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"The sum of 3 and 4 is: "</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// this works because we forward declared add() above</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-10"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-11">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-12"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// even though the body of add() isn't defined until here</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-13"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-14"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f478558804239-15"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0023 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Now when the compiler reaches add() in main, it will know what add() looks like (a function that takes two integer parameters and returns an integer), and it won&#8217;t complain.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that function prototypes do not need to specify the names of the parameters.  In the above code, you can also forward declare your function like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f47f471798536" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f47f471798536-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f47f471798536-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>However, we prefer to name our parameters, because it allows you to understand what the function parameters are just by looking at the prototype.  Otherwise, you&#8217;ll have to locate the actual function definition.</p>
<p><em>Tip: You can easily create function prototypes by using copy/paste on your function declaration.  Don&#8217;t forget the semicolon on the end.</em></p>
<p><strong>Forgetting the function body</strong></p>
<p>One question many new programmers have is: what happens if we forward declare a function but do not define it?</p>
<p>The answer is: it depends.  If a forward declaration is made, but the function is never called, the program will compile and run fine.  However, if a forward declaration is made, the function is called, but the program never defines the function, the program will compile okay, but the linker will complain that it can&#8217;t resolve the function call.</p>
<p>Consider the following program:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f486178481348" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f486178481348-10"><span <!-- [Format Time: 0.0016 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this program, we forward declare add(), and we call add(), but we never define add() anywhere.  When we try and compile this program, Visual Studio 2005 Express produces the following message:</p>
<pre>
Compiling...
add.cpp
Linking...
add.obj : error LNK2001: unresolved external symbol &quot;int __cdecl add(int,int)&quot; (?add@@YAHHH@Z)
add.exe : fatal error LNK1120: 1 unresolved externals
</pre>
<p>As you can see, the program compiled okay, but it failed at the link stage because int add(int, int) was never defined.</p>
<p><strong>Other types of forward declarations</strong></p>
<p>Forward declarations are most often used with functions.  However, forward declarations can also be used with other objects in C++, such as variables (which we discuss in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/42-global-variables/">4.2 -- Global Variables</a>).  We&#8217;ll talk more about how to forward declare other types of objects in future lessons.</p>
<p><strong>Declarations vs definitions</strong></p>
<p>In C++, you&#8217;ll often hear the words &#8220;declaration&#8221; and &#8220;definition&#8221; used.  What do they mean?  You now have enough of a framework to understand the difference between the two.</p>
<p>A <strong>definition</strong> actually implements or instantiates (causes memory to be allocated for) the identifier.  Here are some examples of definitions:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// defines function add()</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-5">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f48e035123934-6"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// instantiates (causes memory to be allocated for) an integer variable named x</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>You can only have one definition per identifier.  A definition is needed to satisfy the linker.</p>
<p>A <strong>declaration</strong> is an statement that defines an identifier (variable or function name) and its type.  Here are some examples of declarations:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e3f495327154809" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f495327154809-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e3f495327154809-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f495327154809-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">y</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// declares a function named "add" that takes two int parameters and returns an int.&nbsp;&nbsp;No body!</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e3f495327154809-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// declares a integer variable named x</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>A declaration is all that is needed to satisfy the compiler.  This is why using a forward declaration is enough to keep the compiler happy.  However, if you forget to include the definition for the identifier, the linker will complain.</p>
<p>You&#8217;ll note that &#8220;int x&#8221; appears in both categories.  In C++, all definitions also serve as declarations.  Since &#8220;int x&#8221; is a definition, it&#8217;s by default a declaration too.  This is the case with most declarations.</p>
<p>However, there are a small subset of declarations that are not definitions, such as function prototypes.  These are called <strong>pure declarations</strong>.  Others types of pure declarations include forward declarations for variables, class declarations, and type declarations (you will encounter these in future lessons, but don&#8217;t need to worry about them now).  You can have as many pure declarations for an identifier as you desire (although having more than one is typically redundant).</p>

<p>For each of the following programs, state whether they fail to compile, fail to link, or compile and link.  If you are not sure, try compiling them!</p>
<p>3)</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div <!-- [Format Time: 0.0027 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p><strong>Quiz Answers</strong><br />
1) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id1706430077'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id1706430077" style="display:none">A function prototype is declaration statement that tells the compiler what a function&#8217;s return type is, what the name of the function is, and what the types of the function parameters are.  A function prototype can be used to forward declare a function.  A forward declaration tells the compiler about the existence of a function (or other type of object) in advance of where it is implemented.</div>
<p>2) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id1850917905'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id1850917905" style="display:none">
<pre>
// Either of these is correct.
// Do not forget the semicolon on the end, since these are statements.
int doMath(int first, int second, int third, int fourth); // better solution
int doMath(int, int, int, int);
</pre>
</div>
<p>3) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id463957550'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id463957550" style="display:none">Doesn&#8217;t compile.  The compiler will complain that the add() called in main() does not have the same number of parameters as the one that was forward declared.</div>
<p>4) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id1086580862'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id1086580862" style="display:none">Doesn&#8217;t compile.  The compiler will complain that the add() called in main() does not have the same number of parameters as the one that was forward declared. </div>
<p>5) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id1647170828'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id1647170828" style="display:none">Doesn&#8217;t link.  The compiler will match the forward declared prototype of add to the function call to add() in main().  However, no add() function that takes two parameters was ever implemented (we only implemented one that took 3 parameters), so the linker will complain.</div>
<p>6) <a class="solution_link_show" href="javascript:void(0)" onclick="wpSolutionToggle(document.getElementById('id1967397590'), this, 'Show Solution', 'Hide Solution')">Show Solution</a></p>
<div class="solution_div" id="id1967397590" style="display:none">Compiles and links.  The function call to add() matches the prototype that was forward declared, the the implemented function also matches.</div>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=4372#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-4372", "4372", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>GovZ,</p>
<p>Forward declarations are used only to tell the compiler about the existence of a function (or class or variable) before it is actually implemented.</p>
<p>This information is only used during compile time.  Consequently, forward declarations will not make your executables larger or slower.</p>
		</div>

		<p>stdafx.cpp is a file that Microsoft compilers use to do precompiled headers (which makes you program compile faster), if you sent them up correctly.  If you don&#8217;t want to deal with stdafx.h, you can always turn precompiled headers off (in the project settings).</p>

		<p>Many (most?) compilers let you get away with using void main() instead of int main(), and they will implicitly return 0 when you do this.  However, it&#8217;s not technically part of the language, so I avoid it in my examples.</p>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-33903">
		<div id="div-comment-33903" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-33903">
		December 7, 2008 at 11:01 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=33903#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-33903", "33903", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Good question!  It turns out that the variable names in your forward declarations don&#8217;t have to match those in the actual definitions.  This is because the variable names in the forward declarations simply aren&#8217;t used -- only the types are.  You can even omit the variable names from the forward declaration altogether if you want.</p>
<p>However, I think it&#8217;s generally good practice to put them in.  If you see a forward declaration like this:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e45d3e890734189" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e45d3e890734189-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e45d3e890734189-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">doSomething</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">bool</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// what does this bool mean?</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It&#8217;s a lot less meaningful than if you see this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e45d49326038065" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e45d49326038065-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e45d49326038065-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">doSomething</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-t">bool</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">bSilentMode</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// now we have an idea</span></div></div></td>

		<p>So a function prototype is a kind of forward declaration?</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-35429">
		<div id="div-comment-35429" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-35429">
		December 22, 2008 at 11:29 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=35429#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-35429", "35429", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It&#8217;s more accurate to say that one use of function prototypes is for forward declarations.  Function prototypes can also be used in header files and in class declarations (covered in chapter 8).  So function prototypes have more uses than just as forward declarations.</p>
		</div>

		<p>Can we say the forward declaration in nothing but declaring the function globally, where as function prototyping is declaring function locally i.e, in the main function? is that only the difference? <ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-36327">
		<div id="div-comment-36327" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-36327">
		January 3, 2009 at 6:56 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=36327#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-36327", "36327", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>A forward declaration is a specific type of function prototype that allows you to declare a function before you actually define it.  Unfortunately, there&#8217;s no way to &#8220;hide&#8221; such functions from &#8220;outsiders&#8221; -- even if you don&#8217;t declare a function prototype, someone who wanted to use your function could write a function prototype for it and then use it.</p>
<p>The only way to hide functions is to put them inside classes, which we&#8217;ll cover much later in this tutorial.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

<p>1. The first line is missing a closing quotation mark (&#8220;) at the end (it should be &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;).</p>
<p>2. The second include statement does not include anything. I think you meant to include iostream, therefore it should read:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e44532662589825" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0023 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>As the tutorial has stated earlier the program is running line by line so the function add would be unrecognized when it is called while add() is declared later on.</p>
<p>On this example I would actually realize that we have created add() called it in main BUT we never reach the line where return x+y was written down.</p>
<p>Basically I would expect a link error since the call ends up without returning anything?</p>
<p>So my question is why does the program knows that add() returns the value x+y when it shouldn&#8217;t reach that declaration?</p>
<p>Hope someone can understand this, i am German my English certainly lacks a bit.</p>
<p>Thanks<br />
Florian</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-73273">
		<div id="div-comment-73273" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/82fbdd110c1b25f96aadcf5190f11728?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/82fbdd110c1b25f96aadcf5190f11728?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Eugene</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-73273">
		November 28, 2009 at 11:35 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=73273#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-73273", "73273", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Eugene'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Not quite. The prototype does not get overwritten. Rather, the forward declaration informs the compiler of how a call of that function should look like, and thus the compiler can do the necessary setup and translate the function call into assembly/machine code.</p>
<p>The function definition defines the code that will be executed when the function is called. In this case it is in the same source file as the function call, but it could be in a different source file, or might not even be available at all, e.g., just the object code is available in a shared library.</p>
<p>That said, some functions whose function definitions are available might be inlined, i.e., the function call is replaced by the code of the function itself.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

				</table>
			</div>
		</div>

<p></p>

		December 7, 2010 at 8:58 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=95014#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-95014", "95014", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Liquidcool'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Rule 1:   	First perform any calculations inside parentheses.<br />
Rule 2:   	Next perform all multiplications and divisions, working from left to right.<br />
Rule 3:   	Lastly, perform all additions and subtractions, working from left to right.</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>Hi all,</p>
<p>I would like to ask what is the reasoning of c++ creators for forward declaration? Why isnt the compiler designed in such a manner so as to look for a function definition regardless of it being before or after the actual function calling?<br />
I would imagine that it is enough that the function definition resided in the same scope of the function call.<br />
Would the above (my) logic effect the efficiency of the executable or just the compilation?</p>
<p>Thanks in advance</p>
<p>very nice site btw, good job admins <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251249">
		<div id="div-comment-251249" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-251249">
		January 25, 2015 at 2:25 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=251249#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251249", "251249", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>C++ was developed a long time ago when computers were slow and memory was expensive.  I suspect this limitation was done for efficiency/simplicity, so the compiler doesn&#8217;t have to parse the file more than once, or maintain memory-intensive lookup tables for all function calls.</p>
<p>More modern languages (like C#) allow you to declare functions in any order without forward declarations.  It&#8217;s unfortunate that C++ hasn&#8217;t added this.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span 		</div>

<p>It tells me add() can&#8217;t take 2 arguments, and forces me to declare </p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<p>Your forward declaration of add has no parameters, but your definition of add has two.  There&#8217;s a mismatch there that&#8217;s causing the problem.  Fix the forward declaration so it has two parameters.</p>

		October 8, 2011 at 4:14 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=96109#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-96109", "96109", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to zingmars'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>If you only make a forward declaration and never actually make the function the program never actually makes the function, meaning you will get errors when you&#8217;re trying to use the forward declaration.<br />
No you don&#8217;t need a return value to declare a function (void), it just needs to be declared somewhere (it doesn&#8217;t even need to have code in it).</p>
		</div>

		<div id="crayon-555d775e433af795199155" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e433af795199155-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e433af795199155-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0003 seconds] -->
<p> is a definition.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251412">
		<div id="div-comment-251412" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-251412">
		February 7, 2015 at 3:35 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=251412#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251412", "251412", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>int x; is a definition (and a declaration).  A definition defines how something is implemented -- in the case of variables, it&#8217;s probably more intuitive to say it instantiates the variable (causes memory to be allocated for it).</p>
<p>One way to tell it&#8217;s a definition is to duplicate the line and see if the compiler complains (remember, things can only have one definition.</p>
<p>If you do this:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d775e432fa016876437" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e432fa016876437-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d775e432fa016876437-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d775e432fa016876437-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d775e432fa016876437-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">x</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0003 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The compiler will complain.</p>
<p>Although we haven&#8217;t covered it yet, it is possible to forward declare variables.  In that case, the forward declaration is a declaration only (and does not allocate memory -- it just tells the compiler that a variable exists, but it&#8217;s defined elsewhere).</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve updated the lesson text to be more clear about what definition means for variables.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-251552">
		<div id="div-comment-251552" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/b9eae564a77589e64b80d8a71bbc7db9?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Catreece</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-251552">
		February 18, 2015 at 8:32 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=251552#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251552", "251552", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Catreece'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Handy information! A few things I was wondering about, though. And then I tested them because I realized I could answer my own questions. Huh. Well here&apos;s the answers in case anyone else is interested, then. =P</p>
<p>#1: Does the int add(x, y) always have to be NAMED add(x, y)?</p>
<p>I&apos;ve tested and found I can call it addmoose(x, y) without issue.</p>
<p>#2: Does the &quot;add&quot; part NEED to be part of it?</p>
<p>moose(x, y) works just fine, apparently the &quot;add&quot; part is just there for good housekeeping and labeling.</p>
<p>#3: can I have multiple functions named the same thing with different parameters?</p>
<p>Yes and no I found out. I tried messing around with an add and a multiply function to test where the limits were, this is what I came up with:</p>
<p>moose(x, y)<br />
moose(Na, Nb)</p>
<p>Did not work. As far as it was concerned, the x/y and Na/Nb were identical; what they&apos;re called doesn&apos;t matter, only the number of parameters.</p>
<p>moose(x, y)<br />
moose(Na, Nb, Nc)</p>
<p>Did work. It doesn&apos;t seem to matter that you call it the same thing, so long as it can differentiate between moose(2 parameters) and moose(3 parameters). No, I don&apos;t know why I used moose.</p>
<p>#4: Is it a good idea to name functions the same thing?</p>
<p>Depends on the situation, I think. I guess if you&apos;re multiplying several different things, you could call several functions multiply and just alter the number of parameters. Since they&apos;re reusable in different contexts, and multiplying 3 parameters tends to work exactly the same no matter which parameter is being multiplied, so long as you have 3 of them, I suppose it&apos;s not that big of a deal.</p>
<p>On the other hand, it&apos;s handy to name more complex functions to be clear about exactly what it is they&apos;re supposed to do. add(2 parameters) is pretty obvious that it adds two parameters together, so isn&apos;t exactly a big deal if you have add(x, y) and add(x, y, z).</p>
<p>If you&apos;re trying something more complex, such as&#8230; pft, I dunno, something like &quot;F = (D* (((E+Y)*(X/N)) *0.01) / (1+0.01* ((E+Y)*(X/N)))&quot;, then you might want to stick to a somewhat more descriptive title for the function. You COULD reuse totalNonsense(D, E, X, Y, N) with totalNonsense(X, Y, Z), but I wouldn&apos;t particularly suggest it due to issues of confusion.</p>
<p>Anyway, just the random stuff I came up with when trying to figure out some exceptions to the rules. =3</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">

		<p>Regarding your point #3, C++ supports a concept called &#8220;function overloading&#8221;, whereby you can have multiple functions with the same name so long as no two functions have the same number of parameters of the same type in the same order.  I tackle this topic in more detail in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/76-function-overloading/" rel="nofollow">7.6 -- Function overloading</a>.</p>
<p>You&#8217;ll note the following does compile (we haven&#8217;t introduced double yet, but it&#8217;s a numeric data type like int):</p>

<p>Regarding your point 4: as long as the use of the name is intuitive, there&#8217;s no problem using the same function name for more than one thing.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=251930#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251930", "251930", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Daniel Ricci'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>A function prototype is declaration statement that tells the compiler what a functions return type is, what the name of the function is, and what the types of the function parameters are. A function prototype can be used to forward declare a function. A forward declaration tells the compiler about the existence of a function (or other type of object) in advance of where it is implemented.</p>
<p>- I dont think there is a difference in terms of its usage.&nbsp;&nbsp;Declaring a prototype is the act of forward declaring.</p>
		</div>

<p></p>
<p>I declared a function two times with same name,number of arguments, and data type but the compiler didn&#8217;t give an error.Why?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252095">
		<div id="div-comment-252095" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-252095">
		April 8, 2015 at 8:57 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=252095#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252095", "252095", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Declaring an identifier more than once is not illegal.  It&#8217;s just redundant.</p>
<p>Note that you can only define your function once.  If you try to define it more than once, your compiler will complain.</p>

		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/03b50aed88613d87bb6c2c7ef012567d?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/03b50aed88613d87bb6c2c7ef012567d?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">kevin wiggins</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-252391">
		May 10, 2015 at 10:15 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=252391#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252391", "252391", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to kevin wiggins'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>why is that variable declaration cause memory allocation and forward declaration does not for variables?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252397">
		<div id="div-comment-252397" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/#comment-252397">
		May 10, 2015 at 5:50 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/17-forward-declarations/?replytocom=252397#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252397", "252397", "respond", "28" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Variable declarations are also variable definitions.  We use these to tell the compiler that we need a variable to be allocated in memory at this point in the code.</p>
<p>Forward declarations are pure declarations (not definitions), so no memory needs to be allocated for them.  Forward declarations just let the compiler know that something exists.  They don&#8217;t allocate memory for that thing.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
